<th><b>MLS</b></th>
<th><a href="/wiki/Saint_Louis_FC" title="Saint Louis FC">USL</a></th>
<th><a href="/wiki/Chicago_Fire_U-23" title="Chicago Fire U-23">PDL</a></th>

</table>
<p><b>Chicago Fire Soccer Club</b> is an American professional <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">soccer</a> club based in the <a href="/wiki/Chicago" title="Chicago">Chicago</a> suburb of <a href="/wiki/Bridgeview,_Illinois" title="Bridgeview, Illinois">Bridgeview, Illinois</a>. The team competes in <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Soccer" title="Major League Soccer">Major League Soccer</a> (MLS) as a member of the league's <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Conference_(MLS)" title="Eastern Conference (MLS)">Eastern Conference</a>. The franchise is named after the <a href="/wiki/Great_Chicago_Fire" title="Great Chicago Fire">Great Chicago Fire</a> of 1871, and was founded on October 8, 1997, the event's 126th anniversary. The team began play in 1998 as one of the league's first expansion teams. The Fire won the <a href="/wiki/MLS_Cup" title="MLS Cup">MLS Cup</a> as well as the <a href="/wiki/Lamar_Hunt_U.S._Open_Cup" title="Lamar Hunt U.S. Open Cup">U.S. Open Cup</a> (the <a href="/wiki/Double_(association_football)" title="Double (association football)">"double"</a>) on their first season. They have also won U.S. Open Cups in 2000, 2003, and 2006; in addition to the 2003 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MLS_Supporters%27_Shield" title="MLS Supporters' Shield">MLS Supporters' Shield</a>.</p>
<p>The Fire maintains an extensive development system, consisting of the <a href="/wiki/Chicago_Fire_U-23" title="Chicago Fire U-23">Chicago Fire U-23</a> (<a href="/wiki/Premier_Development_League" title="Premier Development League">Premier Development League</a> and <a href="/wiki/Super-20_League" title="Super-20 League">Super-20 League</a> teams), the Chicago Fire Development Academy, and the Chicago Fire Juniors youth organization. They also operate the Chicago Fire Foundation, the team's community-based charitable division. <a href="/wiki/Toyota_Park" title="Toyota Park">Toyota Park</a> is the Fire's home stadium.</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chicago_Fire_Soccer_Club&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Overview">Overview</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chicago_Fire_Soccer_Club&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Overview">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Founded on October 8, 1997,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup> the club was originally based at <a href="/wiki/Soldier_Field" title="Soldier Field">Soldier Field</a>. Since 2006, they reside at <a href="/wiki/Toyota_Park" title="Toyota Park">Toyota Park</a> at 71st and Harlem Avenue in <a href="/wiki/Bridgeview,_Illinois" title="Bridgeview, Illinois">Bridgeview</a>. The owners of the Fire are <a href="/wiki/Andell_Holdings" title="Andell Holdings">Andell Holdings</a>, who purchased the club in 2007. Andell Holdings chairman <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Hauptman" title="Andrew Hauptman">Andrew Hauptman</a> acts as club chairman, while the general manager is Nelson Rodriguez and the chief operating officer is <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Atul_Khosla&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Atul Khosla (page does not exist)">Atul Khosla</a>. The Fire are historically most successful in the <a href="/wiki/Lamar_Hunt_U.S._Open_Cup" title="Lamar Hunt U.S. Open Cup">U.S. Open Cup</a>; winning championships in 1998, 2000, 2003, and 2006. The Fire keeps a close connection with the <a href="/wiki/Chicago_Sting" title="Chicago Sting">Chicago Sting</a> (its predecessor team in the <a href="/wiki/North_American_Soccer_League_(1968%E2%80%9384)" title="North American Soccer League (1968–84)">NASL</a>) by holding frequent commemorative events, reunions, and wearing Sting-inspired shirts.</p>
<p>Many notable players have worn the Fire shirt, including U.S. internationals <a href="/wiki/Chris_Armas" title="Chris Armas">Chris Armas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Bocanegra" title="Carlos Bocanegra">Carlos Bocanegra</a>, <a href="/wiki/Frank_Klopas" title="Frank Klopas">Frank Klopas</a>, <a href="/wiki/DaMarcus_Beasley" title="DaMarcus Beasley">DaMarcus Beasley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brian_McBride" title="Brian McBride">Brian McBride</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tony_Sanneh" title="Tony Sanneh">Tony Sanneh</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cory_Gibbs" title="Cory Gibbs">Cory Gibbs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ante_Razov" title="Ante Razov">Ante Razov</a>, <a href="/wiki/Josh_Wolff" title="Josh Wolff">Josh Wolff</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eric_Wynalda" title="Eric Wynalda">Eric Wynalda</a>. Some of the club's other notable American professional players include <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/C.J._Brown" title="C.J. Brown">C.J. Brown</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jesse_Marsch" title="Jesse Marsch">Jesse Marsch</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chris_Rolfe" title="Chris Rolfe">Chris Rolfe</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Zach_Thornton" title="Zach Thornton">Zach Thornton</a>. The Fire also has a reputation for importing international talent, from established veterans like <a href="/wiki/P%C3%A1vel_Pardo" title="Pável Pardo">Pável Pardo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Piotr_Nowak" title="Piotr Nowak">Piotr Nowak</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cuauht%C3%A9moc_Blanco" title="Cuauhtémoc Blanco">Cuauhtémoc Blanco</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tomasz_Frankowski" title="Tomasz Frankowski">Tomasz Frankowski</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lubos_Kubik" title="Lubos Kubik">Lubos Kubik</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hristo_Stoichkov" title="Hristo Stoichkov">Hristo Stoichkov</a>; in addition to younger players such as <a href="/wiki/Patrick_Nyarko" title="Patrick Nyarko">Patrick Nyarko</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marco_Pappa" title="Marco Pappa">Marco Pappa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Damani_Ralph" title="Damani Ralph">Damani Ralph</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bakary_Soumar%C3%A9" title="Bakary Soumaré">Bakary Soumaré</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nery_Castillo" title="Nery Castillo">Nery Castillo</a>.</p>
<p>The Chicago Fire were named after The Great Chicago Fire that happened in 1871.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foundation_and_initial_success_.281997.E2.80.932000.29">Foundation and initial success (1997–2000)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chicago_Fire_Soccer_Club&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Foundation and initial success (1997–2000)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Chicago_Fire_versus_Dallas_Burn_(JUL-1998).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="799" data-file-width="1195" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Chicago_Fire_versus_Dallas_Burn_%28JUL-1998%29.jpg/220px-Chicago_Fire_versus_Dallas_Burn_%28JUL-1998%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Chicago_Fire_versus_Dallas_Burn_%28JUL-1998%29.jpg/330px-Chicago_Fire_versus_Dallas_Burn_%28JUL-1998%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Chicago_Fire_versus_Dallas_Burn_%28JUL-1998%29.jpg/440px-Chicago_Fire_versus_Dallas_Burn_%28JUL-1998%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Chicago_Fire_versus_Dallas_Burn_(JUL-1998).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Fire (in red) at home to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dallas_Burn" title="Dallas Burn">Dallas Burn</a> in July 1998</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Founded in 1997 at <a href="/wiki/Navy_Pier" title="Navy Pier">Navy Pier</a>, on the anniversary of the <a href="/wiki/Great_Chicago_Fire" title="Great Chicago Fire">Great Fire</a>, the Fire immediately tapped into the diverse ethnic makeup of the city. The team brought in Polish players <a href="/wiki/Piotr_Nowak" title="Piotr Nowak">Piotr Nowak</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jerzy_Podbrozny" title="Jerzy Podbrozny">Jerzy Podbrozny</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Roman_Kosecki" title="Roman Kosecki">Roman Kosecki</a>; the Mexican <a href="/wiki/Jorge_Campos" title="Jorge Campos">Jorge Campos</a>; and the Czech <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lubos_Kubik" title="Lubos Kubik">Lubos Kubik</a>. While all showed their talent while playing for Chicago that first year, American players (<a href="/wiki/Zach_Thornton" title="Zach Thornton">Zach Thornton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chris_Armas" title="Chris Armas">Chris Armas</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/C.J._Brown" title="C.J. Brown">C.J. Brown</a>) proved most integral to the Fire's continued success. Under the club's first head coach, <a href="/wiki/Bob_Bradley" title="Bob Bradley">Bob Bradley</a>—and against all expectation—the team completed the double in its first competitive year, beating <a href="/wiki/D.C._United" title="D.C. United">D.C. United</a> in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MLS_Cup_1998" title="MLS Cup 1998">1998 MLS Cup Final</a>, and defeating the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Columbus_Crew" title="Columbus Crew">Columbus Crew</a> in Chicago to win the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1998_Lamar_Hunt_U.S._Open_Cup" title="1998 Lamar Hunt U.S. Open Cup">1998 U.S. Open Cup</a> a week later.</p>
<p>The team's momentum continued, reaching the <a href="/wiki/MLS_Cup_2000" title="MLS Cup 2000">2000 MLS Cup final</a> <i>(losing to Kansas City)</i> and winning the <a href="/wiki/2000_Lamar_Hunt_U.S._Open_Cup" title="2000 Lamar Hunt U.S. Open Cup">2000 U.S. Open Cup</a>. Internationally experienced players such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hristo_Stoitchkov" title="Hristo Stoitchkov">Hristo Stoitchkov</a> joined the Fire, while young American talents such as <a href="/wiki/DaMarcus_Beasley" title="DaMarcus Beasley">DaMarcus Beasley</a> developed. The Fire quickly became cemented as one of the league's preeminent teams.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Nomadic_times_.282002.E2.80.932004.29">Nomadic times (2002–2004)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chicago_Fire_Soccer_Club&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Nomadic times (2002–2004)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>With Soldier Field undergoing massive renovations, the Fire moved to the western Chicago suburb of <a href="/wiki/Naperville,_Illinois" title="Naperville, Illinois">Naperville, Illinois</a> in 2002. That same year, Bob Bradley abruptly departed the team to lead the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MetroStars" title="MetroStars">MetroStars</a>, from his home state of <a href="/wiki/New_Jersey" title="New Jersey">New Jersey</a>. The Fire then selected the <a href="/wiki/United_States_men%27s_national_soccer_team" title="United States men's national soccer team">U.S. men's national team's</a> top assistant, <a href="/wiki/Dave_Sarachan" title="Dave Sarachan">Dave Sarachan</a>, to assume the vacant post.</p>
<p>Chicago qualified for <a href="/wiki/MLS_Cup_2003" title="MLS Cup 2003">the league final</a> while also capturing the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MLS_Supporters%27_Shield" title="MLS Supporters' Shield">Supporters' Shield</a> and <a href="/wiki/2003_Lamar_Hunt_U.S._Open_Cup" title="2003 Lamar Hunt U.S. Open Cup">2003 U.S. Open Cup</a> along the way. The team returned to Chicago and the renovated Soldier Field midway through the 2003 season.</p>
<p>After that season, longtime captain <a href="/wiki/Piotr_Nowak" title="Piotr Nowak">Piotr Nowak</a> retired to take a position in the front office. He departed a year later to become manager of <a href="/wiki/D.C._United" title="D.C. United">D.C. United</a>. In this period new talent emerged, including Jamaican striker <a href="/wiki/Damani_Ralph" title="Damani Ralph">Damani Ralph</a>. Still, stagnating performances and the building strength of the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Conference_(MLS)" title="Eastern Conference (MLS)">Eastern Conference</a> made Chicago's league position ever more tenuous. In 2004, the team missed the league playoffs for the first time in their history.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Turmoil.2C_and_a_permanent_home_.282005.E2.80.932007.29">Turmoil, and a permanent home (2005–2007)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chicago_Fire_Soccer_Club&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Turmoil, and a permanent home (2005–2007)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The 2005 season began with the unexpected dismissal of popular club president <a href="/wiki/Peter_Wilt" title="Peter Wilt">Peter Wilt</a> by then-owners <a href="/wiki/Anschutz_Entertainment_Group" title="Anschutz Entertainment Group">AEG</a>, a move decried by fans, many players, and club staff.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> This came as a shock, given his brokering of a $100m deal to build the Fire a stadium in the collar suburb of <a href="/wiki/Bridgeview,_Illinois" title="Bridgeview, Illinois">Bridgeview</a>. He was immediately replaced by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MetroStars" title="MetroStars">MetroStars</a> executive <a href="/wiki/John_Guppy" title="John Guppy">John Guppy</a>.</p>
<p>Competitively, the season was most notable for the blockbuster visit of <a href="/wiki/A.C._Milan" title="A.C. Milan">Milan</a> from Italy's <a href="/wiki/Serie_A" title="Serie A">Serie A</a>, and the surprising 4–0 away defeat of <a href="/wiki/D.C._United" title="D.C. United">D.C. United</a> in the Eastern Conference Semi-finals.</p>
<p>2006 arrived, and the Fire moved from Soldier Field into its new stadium in Bridgeview, a southwest suburb of Chicago: <a href="/wiki/Toyota_Park" title="Toyota Park">Toyota Park</a>, located at the corner of 71st Street and Harlem Avenue. In its first season, it played host to an unspectacular league campaign; but victory in the <a href="/wiki/2006_Lamar_Hunt_U.S._Open_Cup" title="2006 Lamar Hunt U.S. Open Cup">2006 U.S. Open Cup</a> marked a continuation of the club's successes and promise for the future.</p>
<p>The anxiety to win another league title continued to grow, however. <a href="/wiki/Dave_Sarachan" title="Dave Sarachan">Sarachan</a> entered 2007 (his fifth season in charge) under intense pressure from fans and the administration to produce a league championship. Tension mounted further on April 3, 2007, when the Fire signed <a href="/wiki/Mexico_national_football_team" title="Mexico national football team">Mexico</a> and <a href="/wiki/Club_Am%C3%A9rica" title="Club América">América</a> star <a href="/wiki/Cuauht%C3%A9moc_Blanco" title="Cuauhtémoc Blanco">Cuauhtémoc Blanco</a> to a <a href="/wiki/Designated_Player_Rule" title="Designated Player Rule">Designated Player</a> contract. After a perfect three matches to open the year, they won only one of their next eight, and Sarachan was dismissed. Following a brief search, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Club_Deportivo_Los_Millonarios" title="Club Deportivo Los Millonarios">Millionarios</a> manager <a href="/wiki/Juan_Carlos_Osorio" title="Juan Carlos Osorio">Juan Carlos Osorio</a> was named the club's third head coach.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="New_ownership_.282007.E2.80.932009.29">New ownership (2007–2009)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chicago_Fire_Soccer_Club&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: New ownership (2007–2009)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Chicago_Fire_2007_season_night_game.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1856" data-file-width="2784" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Chicago_Fire_2007_season_night_game.JPG/220px-Chicago_Fire_2007_season_night_game.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Chicago_Fire_2007_season_night_game.JPG/330px-Chicago_Fire_2007_season_night_game.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Chicago_Fire_2007_season_night_game.JPG/440px-Chicago_Fire_2007_season_night_game.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Chicago_Fire_2007_season_night_game.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A home game at <a href="/wiki/Toyota_Park" title="Toyota Park">Toyota Park</a> in 2007</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>More change came soon afterward. On September 6, 2007, <a href="/wiki/Andell_Holdings" title="Andell Holdings">Andell Holdings</a>, a Los Angeles-based private investment firm controlled by chairman <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Hauptman" title="Andrew Hauptman">Andrew Hauptman</a>, acquired <a href="/wiki/Anschutz_Entertainment_Group" title="Anschutz Entertainment Group">AEG</a>'s interest in the Chicago Fire Soccer Club. Reports estimated the purchase price to be upwards of $35 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup> The team has not won a major trophy since Hauptman bought the team.</p>
<p>On the field, behind Blanco and <a href="/wiki/Wilman_Conde" title="Wilman Conde">Wilman Conde</a>, Osorio's central defender at Millionarios, the Fire went on an extended unbeaten run to close the season, easily qualifying for the playoffs but were defeated at <a href="/wiki/New_England_Revolution" title="New England Revolution">New England</a> in the Eastern Conference Final. On December 10, 2007, the Fire announced Osorio's resignation. He was named manager of the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Red_Bulls" title="New York Red Bulls">New York Red Bulls</a> eight days later. Hauptman filed tampering charges with the league in protest, and the Fire were compensated by the Red Bulls with cash and draft picks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<p>Changes came quickly in Osorio's wake. On January 17, 2008, former Fire star <a href="/wiki/Frank_Klopas" title="Frank Klopas">Frank Klopas</a> was named Technical Director in charge of player personnel, and longtime Fire assistant <a href="/wiki/Denis_Hamlett" title="Denis Hamlett">Denis Hamlett</a> was appointed manager. While the Fire struggled at home in <a href="/wiki/2008_Major_League_Soccer_season" title="2008 Major League Soccer season">2008</a> the team found unusual success on the road, gathering 22 out of a possible 45 away points. Momentum grew with the long-anticipated signing of Chicago native <a href="/wiki/Brian_McBride" title="Brian McBride">Brian McBride</a> on a free transfer in July 2008. After disposing of the Red Bulls 5–2 in the season's final game, they decisively conquered New England in the first round of the playoffs with a 3–0 victory at home. This was Chicago's first playoff advancement over the Revolution in four consecutive seasons. But triumph only lasted for a week, as they again missed the league final with their 2–1 Eastern Conference Final loss to eventual champion <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Columbus_Crew" title="Columbus Crew">Columbus</a>.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/2009_Major_League_Soccer_season" title="2009 Major League Soccer season">2009 season</a> saw few alterations to the previous year's roster. The story of the season was much the same, as continued poor home form offset excellent performances away from Toyota Park. This led to a second place Eastern Conference finish behind Columbus. Despite this, <a href="/wiki/Real_Salt_Lake" title="Real Salt Lake">Real Salt Lake</a> managed to upset the Crew in the quarterfinals, meaning Chicago would host the semi-final for the first time in six years. Chicago's nearly flawless home playoff history meant little in the end, as they lost to Salt Lake, 5–3, on penalties after 120 scoreless minutes. Shortly thereafter, manager Denis Hamlett was dismissed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="A_team_in_flux_.282010.E2.80.932012.29">A team in flux (2010–2012)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chicago_Fire_Soccer_Club&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: A team in flux (2010–2012)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Leading up to <a href="/wiki/2010_Major_League_Soccer_season" title="2010 Major League Soccer season">2010</a>, Chicago hired <a href="/wiki/Carlos_de_los_Cobos" title="Carlos de los Cobos">Carlos de los Cobos</a> as head coach, previously manager of <a href="/wiki/El_Salvador_national_football_team" title="El Salvador national football team">El Salvador</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Cuauht%C3%A9moc_Blanco" title="Cuauhtémoc Blanco">Cuauhtémoc Blanco</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chris_Rolfe" title="Chris Rolfe">Chris Rolfe</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gonzalo_Segares" title="Gonzalo Segares">Gonzalo Segares</a> all departed. More changes came in the summer transfer window with the trade of <a href="/wiki/Justin_Mapp" title="Justin Mapp">Justin Mapp</a> to <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_Union" title="Philadelphia Union">Philadelphia</a>, the acquisition of Mexican international striker <a href="/wiki/Nery_Castillo" title="Nery Castillo">Nery Castillo</a>, and the trade for former Swedish international midfielder <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fredrik_Ljungberg" title="Fredrik Ljungberg">Fredrik Ljungberg</a>. Defender <a href="/wiki/Gonzalo_Segares" title="Gonzalo Segares">Gonzalo Segares</a> returned to the Fire, leaving <a href="/wiki/Apollon_Limassol" title="Apollon Limassol">Apollon Limassol</a> after only six months away. Despite these reinforcements, the Fire failed to qualify for the playoffs for only the second time in club history. Former US international <a href="/wiki/Brian_McBride" title="Brian McBride">Brian McBride</a> and club original <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/C.J._Brown" title="C.J. Brown">C.J. Brown</a> retired at season's end, followed closely by the departures of <a href="/wiki/Wilman_Conde" title="Wilman Conde">Wilman Conde</a>, Ljungberg, and Castillo.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/2011_Major_League_Soccer_season" title="2011 Major League Soccer season">2011</a> began much in the way of 2010, with foundering performances both home and away. After nine winless matches, <a href="/wiki/Carlos_de_los_Cobos" title="Carlos de los Cobos">Carlos de los Cobos</a> was let go on May 30, 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> Technical Director <a href="/wiki/Frank_Klopas" title="Frank Klopas">Frank Klopas</a> was named interim head coach. Behind summer reinforcements <a href="/wiki/P%C3%A1vel_Pardo" title="Pável Pardo">Pável Pardo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sebasti%C3%A1n_Grazzini" title="Sebastián Grazzini">Sebastián Grazzini</a>, as well as forward <a href="/wiki/Dominic_Oduro" title="Dominic Oduro">Dominic Oduro</a>'s 12 goals after being acquired in a trade from <a href="/wiki/Houston_Dynamo" title="Houston Dynamo">Houston</a> and Dan Gargan's defensive addition, the Fire qualified for the <a href="/wiki/2011_Lamar_Hunt_U.S._Open_Cup_Final" title="2011 Lamar Hunt U.S. Open Cup Final">US Open Cup Final</a> (lost at <a href="/wiki/Seattle_Sounders_FC" title="Seattle Sounders FC">Seattle</a>) and narrowly missed making the playoffs after gaining 24 points in their last 12 league matches. After the season's conclusion, Klopas was given the permanent manager job on November 3, 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<p>Although expectations were modest for <a href="/wiki/2012_Major_League_Soccer_season" title="2012 Major League Soccer season">2012</a>, Klopas' first full season as coach, the year saw a change in fortune for the Fire. The spring and summer months saw several new acquisitions for the club, starting with the reacquiring of <a href="/wiki/Chris_Rolfe" title="Chris Rolfe">Chris Rolfe</a> from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aalborg_BK" title="Aalborg BK">Aalborg BK</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> Rolfe, who scored eight goals and 12 assists in the 21 games he played in 2012, would later be named the Fire's MVP.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> Other signings included Brazilian midfielders <a href="/wiki/Alex_Monteiro_de_Lima" title="Alex Monteiro de Lima">Alex Monteiro de Lima</a> from the Swiss side <a href="/wiki/FC_Wohlen" title="FC Wohlen">FC Wohlen</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alvaro_Fernandez" title="Alvaro Fernandez">Alvaro Fernandez</a> from <a href="/wiki/Seattle_Sounders_FC" title="Seattle Sounders FC">Seattle Sounders FC</a>, forward <a href="/wiki/Sherjill_MacDonald" title="Sherjill MacDonald">Sherjill MacDonald</a> from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Beerschot_AC" title="Beerschot AC">Beerschot AC</a> of Belgium and veteran defender <a href="/wiki/Arne_Friedrich" title="Arne Friedrich">Arne Friedrich</a> from <a href="/wiki/VfL_Wolfsburg" title="VfL Wolfsburg">VfL Wolfsburg</a>. Although they would fall out of the U.S. Open tournament early that season, the Fire eventually compiled a 17–11–6 record, their best since 2000, and ranked as high as second in the Eastern Conference before ending the year in fourth place.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> On October 31, 2012, in their first playoff appearance since 2009, the Fire lost their first-round <a href="/wiki/MLS_Cup" title="MLS Cup">MLS Cup</a> playoff match-up at home against the <a href="/wiki/Houston_Dynamo" title="Houston Dynamo">Houston Dynamo</a>, 2–1.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Missing_the_playoffs:_2013.E2.80.93present">Missing the playoffs: 2013–present</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chicago_Fire_Soccer_Club&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Missing the playoffs: 2013–present">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In the 2012–2013 offseason, the franchise made some moves to improve on 2012's success. The team acquired <a href="/wiki/Joel_Lindpere" title="Joel Lindpere">Joel Lindpere</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jeff_Larentowicz" title="Jeff Larentowicz">Jeff Larentowicz</a> and also traded <a href="/wiki/Dominic_Oduro" title="Dominic Oduro">Dominic Oduro</a> for <a href="/wiki/Dilly_Duka" title="Dilly Duka">Dilly Duka</a> and the rights to <a href="/wiki/Robbie_Rogers" title="Robbie Rogers">Robbie Rogers</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> The beginning of the season saw the team struggling to score goals, resulting in a record of 2–5–1 through April. After two successive losses to the Union in May, and with veteran <a href="/wiki/Arne_Friedrich" title="Arne Friedrich">Arne Friedrich</a> still on injured reserve, the Fire acquired their former centerback <a href="/wiki/Bakary_Soumar%C3%A9" title="Bakary Soumaré">Bakary Soumaré</a> from Philadelphia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> Also in May, Robbie Rogers expressed an interest to play in Southern California, at which point a deal was brokered for Rogers' rights in exchange for Chicago native <a href="/wiki/Mike_Magee_(soccer)" title="Mike Magee (soccer)">Mike Magee</a> from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Galaxy" title="Los Angeles Galaxy">Los Angeles Galaxy</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> On June 23, 2013, Friedrich, who had not played a 2012–13 game due to recurring injuries, announced his retirement.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> After starting the season 2–7–3, the additions of Soumare and Magee led to seven wins in the squad's last 10 games. The Fire were busy in the transfer window as well, adding veteran defensive midfielder <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Egidio_Ar%C3%A9valo" title="Egidio Arévalo">Arévalo Ríos</a> and forward <a href="/wiki/Juan_Luis_Anangon%C3%B3" title="Juan Luis Anangonó">Juan Luis Anangonó</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> The Chicago Fire also advanced to host the semifinal of the <a href="/wiki/2013_Lamar_Hunt_U.S._Open_Cup" title="2013 Lamar Hunt U.S. Open Cup">2013 Lamar Hunt U.S. Open Cup</a>, but fell 2–0 to eventual champions <a href="/wiki/D.C._United" title="D.C. United">D.C. United</a>. Alleged fan actions in the stadium that night led to a famous editorial piece, "What it means to be a part of the Fire family",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> being penned by the club's Director of Communications, which was seen as an odd attack on the fan base and widely panned by local and national media. After a 12–6–6 finish to the season, the Fire narrowly missed the playoffs for the third time in the last four years—losing out to the Montreal Impact on goal difference. On October 30, 2013, the club announced that the president of soccer operations Javier Leon and head coach <a href="/wiki/Frank_Klopas" title="Frank Klopas">Frank Klopas</a> had stepped down,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> but the Fire front office had a replacement one day later. On October 31, 2013 Chicago Fire named <a href="/wiki/Frank_Yallop" title="Frank Yallop">Frank Yallop</a> as its new head coach and director of soccer.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> On December 5, 2013, Fire MVP Mike Magee became the first Fire player to win the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MLS_MVP_Award" title="MLS MVP Award">MLS MVP Award</a>—beating out <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Galaxy" title="Los Angeles Galaxy">Los Angeles Galaxy</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Robbie_Keane" title="Robbie Keane">Robbie Keane</a> and <a href="/wiki/Montreal_Impact" title="Montreal Impact">Montreal Impact</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Marco_Di_Vaio" title="Marco Di Vaio">Marco Di Vaio</a> for the honor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Magee_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-Magee-22">[22]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup></p>
<p>Meanwhile, Yallop was busy recruiting a new coaching staff which included "Ring of Fire" member and Chicago Fire veteran <a href="/wiki/C._J._Brown" title="C. J. Brown">C. J. Brown</a> and former U.S. International striker <a href="/wiki/Clint_Mathis" title="Clint Mathis">Clint Mathis</a> as the team's assistant coaches, adding Columbus Crew's <a href="/wiki/Brian_Bliss" title="Brian Bliss">Brian Bliss</a> as Technical Director. Former Fire forward <a href="/wiki/Brian_McBride" title="Brian McBride">Brian McBride</a> was added as an assistant coach in May 2014 for a short-term assignment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> The shake-up extended to the roster, as Yallop moved team veterans and starters and brought in youth prospects—reforming the team while freeing up cap space. Major exits in early 2014 included <a href="/wiki/Chris_Rolfe" title="Chris Rolfe">Chris Rolfe</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Austin_Berry_(soccer)" title="Austin Berry (soccer)">Austin Berry</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Jalil_Anibaba" title="Jalil Anibaba">Jalil Anibaba</a>, <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Paladini" title="Daniel Paladini">Daniel Paladini</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Paolo_Tornaghi" title="Paolo Tornaghi">Paolo Tornaghi</a>. Filling that void was a handful of youth prospects including <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Harrison_Shipp" title="Harrison Shipp">Harrison Shipp</a> (<a href="/wiki/Homegrown_Player_Rule_(Major_League_Soccer)" title="Homegrown Player Rule (Major League Soccer)">homegrown player</a>), <a href="/wiki/Benji_Joya" title="Benji Joya">Benji Joya</a> (via MLS "weighted lottery"), and Grant Ward on loan from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tottenham_Hotspur" title="Tottenham Hotspur">Tottenham Hotspur</a>. Despite rarely looking like a team that could advance to the <a href="/wiki/MLS_Cup_Playoffs" title="MLS Cup Playoffs">MLS Cup Playoffs</a>, the team once again advanced to the semifinals of the <a href="/wiki/2014_Lamar_Hunt_U.S._Open_Cup" title="2014 Lamar Hunt U.S. Open Cup">2014 Lamar Hunt U.S. Open Cup</a>, but were routed 6–0 by eventual champions <a href="/wiki/Seattle_Sounders_FC" title="Seattle Sounders FC">Seattle Sounders FC</a> on August 13. The result was the worst competitive defeat in club history and saw Frank Yallop issue an apology to Chicago Fire supporters on the club's official website.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> As the Cup run had, the season ended in disappointment, with the Fire ending the season with a 6–18–10 record, with 18 draws, also setting a record for most draws in an MLS season in the process.</p>
<p>The club began 2015 with renewed hope, bringing three new Designated Player signings in <a href="/wiki/David_Accam" title="David Accam">David Accam</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shaun_Maloney" title="Shaun Maloney">Shaun Maloney</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kennedy_Igboananike" title="Kennedy Igboananike">Kennedy Igboananike</a> to bolster an anemic attack. The club also signed products <a href="/wiki/Michael_Stephens_(soccer)" title="Michael Stephens (soccer)">Michael Stephens</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eric_Gehrig" title="Eric Gehrig">Eric Gehrig</a> as well as Trinindad &amp; Tobago international <a href="/wiki/Joevin_Jones" title="Joevin Jones">Joevin Jones</a>. With so many new pieces needing to adjust, 2015 marked the first time in club history the side began the season with an 0–3–0 record, but they showed signs of recovery by winning their next three matches. Unfortunately, April was the last time the club would be anywhere near equal on wins and losses, but the side did still advance to another <a href="/wiki/2015_Lamar_Hunt_U.S._Open_Cup" title="2015 Lamar Hunt U.S. Open Cup">Lamar Hunt U.S. Open Cup</a> semifinal. Playing in front of a sparse crowd at the <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_Union" title="Philadelphia Union">Philadelphia Union</a>'s <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PPL_Park" title="PPL Park">PPL Park</a>, the Fire fell 1–0 at the same hurdle for the third straight season. Less than two weeks later, Maloney, who was the club's center piece offseason signing, was transferred back to England with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hull_City" title="Hull City">Hull City</a> sighting personal reasons.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup></p>
<p>Despite no hope for a Cup final, widespread fan protests<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> and dim likelihood of a playoff berth, the club didn't part ways with Frank Yallop until September 20, 2015, one day after another listless 1–0 home defeat to <a href="/wiki/Orlando_City_SC" title="Orlando City SC">Orlando City SC</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> Along with Yallop's departure, the club announced it had named long-time MLS executive Nelson Rodriguez as the club's new General Manager, with his first job being to commence a search for a new head coach. Technical director Brian Bliss was given the interim head coaching job, with former player and current club vice president <a href="/wiki/Logan_Pause" title="Logan Pause">Logan Pause</a> assisting for the remaining five matches. The club has finished the 2015 season with an overall record of 8 wins, 20 losses and 6 ties. For the first time in the club's history Fire finished the season with zero road wins (0-12-5). Twenty losses in a season became the highest in the club's history.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup></p>
<p>On November 18, 2015, Rodriguez made his first moves as GM, firing most of Yallop's remaining technical staff, including goalkeeping coach Aron Hyde, fitness coach Adrian Lamb and Director of Scouting Trevor James.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> Rodriguez also parted ways with the club's long-time Director of First Team Operations Ron Stern, Equipment Manager Charles Raycroft and Assistant Equipment Manager Allan Araujo. On November 24, 2015, the club announced that <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Veljko_Paunovic" title="Veljko Paunovic">Veljko Paunovic</a>, former coach of the Serbian U-20 side that won the <a href="/wiki/2015_FIFA_U-20_World_Cup" title="2015 FIFA U-20 World Cup">2015 FIFA U-20 World Cup</a>, had been named the new head coach of the Chicago Fire.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> On January 5, 2016, technical director <a href="/wiki/Brian_Bliss" title="Brian Bliss">Brian Bliss</a> also departed the Fire to join Sporting Kansas City as Director of Player Personnel, completing the total overhaul of the technical staff.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Colors_and_badge">Colors and badge</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chicago_Fire_Soccer_Club&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Colors and badge">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:CHI_Fire_Alternate.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="344" data-file-width="392" height="132" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/6/65/CHI_Fire_Alternate.png/150px-CHI_Fire_Alternate.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/6/65/CHI_Fire_Alternate.png/225px-CHI_Fire_Alternate.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/6/65/CHI_Fire_Alternate.png/300px-CHI_Fire_Alternate.png 2x" width="150"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:CHI_Fire_Alternate.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Chicago Fire alternate logo (1998–2006)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The official club colors are red and white. Over its history, the Fire have also employed navy blue, sky blue, and black as alternate colors.</p>
<p>The Chicago Fire logo is derived from the standard shape of a fire department's crest (also shown by the <a href="/wiki/Chicago_Fire_Department" title="Chicago Fire Department">Chicago Fire Department</a>), also known as a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cross_of_Saint_Florian" title="Cross of Saint Florian">Florian's cross</a>. This style was chosen by the original general manager, Peter Wilt, to establish a timeless image evocative of both classic American sports (as in the logos of the <a href="/wiki/National_Hockey_League" title="National Hockey League">NHL</a> <a href="/wiki/Original_Six" title="Original Six">Original Six</a>) and the traditions of European soccer.</p>
<p>The logo features a stylized 'C' at its heart (representing <a href="/wiki/Chicago" title="Chicago">Chicago</a>), similar to the logos of the <a href="/wiki/Chicago_Bears" title="Chicago Bears">Bears</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chicago_Cubs" title="Chicago Cubs">Cubs</a>. The six points in a ring around the center allude to the stars in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Municipal_Flag_of_Chicago" title="Municipal Flag of Chicago">Municipal Flag of Chicago</a>, specifically the one commemorating the <a href="/wiki/Great_Chicago_Fire" title="Great Chicago Fire">Great Chicago Fire</a> of 1871.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Nike,_Inc." title="Nike, Inc.">Nike</a>, the Fire's original equipment supplier, intended for the team to be named the Chicago Rhythm. The Rhythm identity featured a turquoise, black and green color scheme, and a logo adorned with a <a href="/wiki/Cobra" title="Cobra">cobra</a>. Team officials ignored Nike's work, and privately developed the Fire identity with the help of Adrenalin, Inc., a well-known sports-specific branding agency.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup></p>
<p>The original Fire shirts were chosen because of their resemblance to a Chicago fireman's coat, featuring broad horizontal stripes across the torso and sleeves. In the first year, the home jersey was red and white with a silver "FIRE" on the stripe; while the away shirts were white and black in the same style. The jersey has remained remarkably constant ever since, continually maintaining the same format of an all-red shirt with a white horizontal chest stripe, even through changes in equipment sponsor (from <a href="/wiki/Nike,_Inc." title="Nike, Inc.">Nike</a>, to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Puma_AG" title="Puma AG">Puma</a>, and currently <a href="/wiki/Adidas" title="Adidas">adidas</a>), until 2012 when the white stripe was exchanged for a blue stripe. Conversely, the Fire's secondary shirts have changed much over the years from white with black, to white with navy, to white with red, to all-white style and the all-blue currently used. Third shirts have often been yellow (originally to honor the Chicago Sting, later for the expired partnership with <a href="/wiki/Monarcas_Morelia" title="Monarcas Morelia">Morelia</a>). A popular light blue third shirt was worn in 2005, based on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Municipal_Flag_of_Chicago" title="Municipal Flag of Chicago">Municipal Flag of Chicago</a> but was discontinued during the sponsorship change to <a href="/wiki/Adidas" title="Adidas">Adidas</a> the next year.</p>
<p>The club and their fans make frequent use of the symbols of Chicago, as a show of civic pride. Most prominent are the six-pointed Chicago stars, but the light blue color associated with the city, the municipal device, and the city skyline appear regularly on materials produced by the club and its fans. The <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Chicago" title="Flag of Chicago">municipal flag of Chicago</a> is also favored by fans and often seen at the stadium, in a manner akin to the use of the <a href="/wiki/Senyera" title="Senyera">flag of Catalonia</a> by <a href="/wiki/FC_Barcelona" title="FC Barcelona">FC Barcelona</a> fans but without a nationalist subtext.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Stadium">Stadium</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chicago_Fire_Soccer_Club&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Stadium">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Toyota_Park,_9_March_2013.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2239" data-file-width="3264" height="151" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Toyota_Park%2C_9_March_2013.jpg/220px-Toyota_Park%2C_9_March_2013.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Toyota_Park%2C_9_March_2013.jpg/330px-Toyota_Park%2C_9_March_2013.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Toyota_Park%2C_9_March_2013.jpg/440px-Toyota_Park%2C_9_March_2013.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Toyota_Park,_9_March_2013.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Toyota_Park" title="Toyota Park">Toyota Park</a>, Chicago Fire's home stadium since 2006</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Chicago plays its home games at <a href="/wiki/Toyota_Park" title="Toyota Park">Toyota Park</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Soccer-specific_stadium" title="Soccer-specific stadium">soccer-specific stadium</a> located at 71st Street and Harlem Avenue in the Chicago suburb of <a href="/wiki/Bridgeview,_Illinois" title="Bridgeview, Illinois">Bridgeview, Illinois</a>, about 12 miles southwest from downtown Chicago. The stadium opened on June 11, 2006 and was developed at a cost of around $100 million. The <a href="/wiki/Bridgeview,_Illinois" title="Bridgeview, Illinois">Village of Bridgeview</a> owns and operates <a href="/wiki/Toyota_Park" title="Toyota Park">Toyota Park</a>.</p>
<p>For its first years in the league the Fire played at <a href="/wiki/Soldier_Field" title="Soldier Field">Soldier Field</a>, the 61,500-capacity home of the <a href="/wiki/Chicago_Bears" title="Chicago Bears">Chicago Bears</a> of the <a href="/wiki/National_Football_League" title="National Football League">NFL</a> and one of the main venues of the <a href="/wiki/1994_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1994 FIFA World Cup">1994 FIFA World Cup</a>. While that stadium was undergoing a $632 million renovation, the Fire played at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cardinal_Stadium_(Naperville)" title="Cardinal Stadium (Naperville)">Cardinal Stadium</a> in <a href="/wiki/Naperville,_Illinois" title="Naperville, Illinois">Naperville, Illinois</a>, on the outskirts of the Chicago metropolitan area. They returned to Soldier Field toward the end of 2003, remaining there through the end of 2005.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Home_stadiums">Home stadiums</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chicago_Fire_Soccer_Club&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Home stadiums">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Club_culture">Club culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chicago_Fire_Soccer_Club&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Club culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Supporters">Supporters</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chicago_Fire_Soccer_Club&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Supporters">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Section8Chicago.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="683" data-file-width="1024" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/2/28/Section8Chicago.jpg/220px-Section8Chicago.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/2/28/Section8Chicago.jpg/330px-Section8Chicago.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/2/28/Section8Chicago.jpg/440px-Section8Chicago.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Section8Chicago.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
"Section 8", the supporters area at <a href="/wiki/Toyota_Park" title="Toyota Park">Toyota Park</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">
<div style="width:52px"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/></a></div>
</td>
<td class="mbox-text"><span class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>does not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">cite</a> any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">sources</a></b>. <span class="hide-when-compact">Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Chicago_Fire_Soccer_Club&amp;action=edit">improve this section</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Burden_of_evidence" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">removed</a>.</span> <small><i>(January 2012)</i></small> <small class="hide-when-compact"><i>(<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></span></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>There is a noteworthy fan culture for the Fire, existing from the date the club was founded, and building on an enthusiasm throughout Chicago sports. At matches, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Supporters_groups" title="Supporters groups">supporters</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ultras" title="Ultras">ultras</a> groups occupy a standing area directly behind the north goal, in the <i>Harlem End</i> of <a href="/wiki/Toyota_Park" title="Toyota Park">Toyota Park</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> This area is referred to as <i>Section 8</i>, originating from the numbering of the corresponding section at <a href="/wiki/Soldier_Field" title="Soldier Field">Soldier Field</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Section_8_(military)" title="Section 8 (military)">American military designation</a> of mentally unfit soldiers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Section_8_Chicago" title="Section 8 Chicago">Section 8 Chicago</a>, the Independent Supporters' Association(ISA) for the Fire, oversees the activities of these numerous groups.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> While incorporating a worldwide variety of styles with a Chicago bent, groups as part of <i>Section 8</i> generally fall under the ultras designation. Additionally, an associated spinoff group called "Sector Latino" congregates in the corner-kick Section 101 at the stadium's southwest end.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Section_8_Chicago" title="Section 8 Chicago">Section 8 Chicago</a> ISA is a registered 501(c)7 non-profit organization run by volunteers through an elected board of directors.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup></p>
<p>Match atmosphere is known for organized displays of stadium-wide support, particularly for matches of prime competitive importance. Call-and-response cheering amongst the crowd is commonplace.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> Fans at Toyota Park for Fire matches periodically choreograph <a href="/wiki/Tifo" title="Tifo">tifo</a> presentations both to show their pride and inspire the players on the field.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> Toyota Park remains one of the few American environments to conduct such fan-driven presentations on a large scale.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mascot">Mascot</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chicago_Fire_Soccer_Club&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Mascot">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Their official mascot is Sparky, an anthropomorphic <a href="/wiki/Dalmatian_(dog)" title="Dalmatian (dog)">Dalmatian</a> dog. Sparky is usually shown wearing the club's jersey but also arrives wearing firefighter attire.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sparky_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-Sparky-49">[49]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rivalries">Rivalries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chicago_Fire_Soccer_Club&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Rivalries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>While the Fire have heated rivalries with a number of different MLS teams, Fire supporters of different ages will likely give different responses as to who the club's main rival is. The earliest Fire supporters would list <a href="/wiki/Brimstone_Cup" title="Brimstone Cup">Brimstone Cup</a> rival <a href="/wiki/FC_Dallas" title="FC Dallas">FC Dallas</a> as the Fire's nemesis, or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Galaxy" title="Los Angeles Galaxy">Los Angeles Galaxy</a> following heated playoff and cup matches with Dallas and L.A. in the league's early years.</p>
<p>After the Fire moved to the Eastern Conference, meetings with Dallas and LA became less frequent. Rivalries with <a href="/wiki/D.C._United" title="D.C. United">D.C. United</a> and <a href="/wiki/New_England_Revolution" title="New England Revolution">New England Revolution</a> were stoked following several thrilling playoff meetings. The Fire and Revolution are MLS' most frequent playoff matchup, meeting in the MLS Cup Playoffs 8 different times in 10 seasons from 2000 to 2009, splitting those encounters 4–4, with the Fire winning in 2000, 2003, 2008, and 2009. New England ended the Fire's playoff runs in 2002, 2005, 2006, and 2007. Newer rivals include <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Columbus_Crew" title="Columbus Crew">Columbus Crew</a>, who are the closest MLS team geographically to the Fire, and <a href="/wiki/New_York_Red_Bulls" title="New York Red Bulls">New York Red Bulls</a> following the departure of former Fire head coach Juan Carlos Osorio to New York in 2007.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Broadcasting">Broadcasting</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chicago_Fire_Soccer_Club&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Broadcasting">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Fire matches are televised locally on <a href="/wiki/Comcast_SportsNet_Chicago" title="Comcast SportsNet Chicago">Comcast SportsNet Chicago</a>. <a href="/wiki/Dan_P._Kelly" title="Dan P. Kelly">Dan Kelly</a> and former Fire coach <a href="/wiki/Frank_Klopas" title="Frank Klopas">Frank Klopas</a> provide play-by-play and color commentary, respectively.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> Matches were previously televised by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NBC_Chicago_Nonstop" title="NBC Chicago Nonstop">NBC Chicago Nonstop</a> and <a href="/wiki/WPWR-TV" title="WPWR-TV">WPWR-TV</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> Select matches featuring the Chicago Fire are nationally broadcast on <a href="/wiki/ESPN" title="ESPN">ESPN</a>, <a href="/wiki/ESPN2" title="ESPN2">ESPN2</a>, <a href="/wiki/UniM%C3%A1s" title="UniMás">UniMás</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fox_Sports_1" title="Fox Sports 1">Fox Sports 1</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Univision" title="Univision">Univision</a> via the league's television agreements.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2015, the Chicago Fire and Comcast SportsNet Chicago agreed to a three-year deal, which includes 21 regular season and postseason matches for 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2016, the Chicago Fire and <a href="/wiki/Tribune_Broadcasting" title="Tribune Broadcasting">Tribune Broadcasting</a> agreed to a three-year deal, which will see all regular season and postseason matches broadcast on <a href="/wiki/WGN_(AM)" title="WGN (AM)">WGN Radio</a> and their <a href="/wiki/Internet_radio" title="Internet radio">internet-only sister station</a> WGN Plus starting in the <a href="/wiki/2017_Major_League_Soccer_season" title="2017 Major League Soccer season">2017 MLS season</a>.</p>

<tr class="vcard agent">
<td style="text-align: center">2</td>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ring_of_Fire">Ring of Fire</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chicago_Fire_Soccer_Club&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Ring of Fire">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The "Ring of Fire" was established in 2003 by Chicago Fire Soccer Club and the Chicago Fire Alumni Association as permanent tribute to honor those who have made the club proud and successful over its history.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> Aside from the initial member <a href="/wiki/Piotr_Nowak" title="Piotr Nowak">Piotr Nowak</a>, only "Ring of Fire" members can select new inductees, and no more than one can be selected any year. Names and numbers (if applicable) are prominently displayed inside <a href="/wiki/Toyota_Park" title="Toyota Park">Toyota Park</a>.</p>
<p>There were no inductees in 2008, 2010, or 2011. In 2008, the members voted to honor two recently deceased fans (supporter leaders Dan Parry and Brandon Kitchens) but were overruled by the club chairman <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Hauptman" title="Andrew Hauptman">Andrew Hauptman</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> Parry and Kitchens were later made members of the Wall of Honor, a special recognition for Fire fans. In addition to Parry and Kitchens, the late Fire fans Euan McLean and Al Hack have been inducted into the Wall of Honor as of 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/C.J._Brown" title="C.J. Brown">C.J. Brown</a> was expected to be honored in 2011, but a new rule was established that inductees must have been away from the club for at least a calendar year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> Brown, at the time an assistant head coach at Real Salt Lake, was officially inducted at the halftime ceremony during the home game vs. Real Salt Lake in Toyota Park on May 9, 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup></p>
<p>On October 3, 2015, <a href="/wiki/Ante_Razov" title="Ante Razov">Ante Razov</a>, the club's all-time leading scorer, became the eight individual to be inducted into the club's Ring of Fire Hall of Fame.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> The ceremony took place on that day during the halftime of the regular season home match against New England Revolution.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup></p>

<li><a href="/wiki/Chicago_Fire_Juniors" title="Chicago Fire Juniors">Chicago Fire Juniors</a> – Local (U8 to U23 Youth Club) with three Chicago branches; satellite clubs in Indiana, Louisville (Kentucky), Florida, Michigan, Louisiana, and Mississippi.</li>
<li>Indiana Fire Academy – Satellite (U-12, U-13, U-14, U-15, U-16, U-18) Academy club in the United States Soccer Development Academy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup></li>
